## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks the stress-strain-temperature relationship, a fundamental constitutive law in materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic moduli and flow stress, while strain governs the mechanical response through linear or nonlinear relationships.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Nonlinear temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (exponential thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic combined response)
- Johnson-Cook strength term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)**c4 (full JC without strain rate)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1 / T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Polynomial stress-strain with thermal coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (quadratic with T-dependent coefficients)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Ludwik power law with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (1 / T))) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo model)
- Cubic stress-strain (hyperelastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**3 (odd-power expansion for symmetric response)
- Combined polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 + c3 * T * epsilon (general polynomial constitutive law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) multiplying strain-dependent terms
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress plateau
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 for work-hardening metals in plastic regime
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) factors coupling temperature to mechanical response
- Odd-function symmetry in strain → stress as odd function of strain (only odd powers: epsilon, epsilon**3, ...) for symmetric tension-compression behavior
- Temperature-strain separability → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), multiplicative decomposition common in constitutive models
- Phase transition or abrupt softening → sigmoidal or step-like temperature dependence indicating critical temperature behavior
- Rubber-like hyperelasticity → terms combining epsilon and 1/epsilon (or epsilon**(-2)) from strain energy derivatives
